Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\\n7: \\n8: BUG FIXES:\\n9: \\n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\\n12: - Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n13: - Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\\n14:   ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\\n15: - Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\\n16: - Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\\n23: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\\n32: \\n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n34: \\n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. **Ephemeral resources**: Ephemeral resources are read anew during each phase of Terraform evaluation, and cannot be persisted to state storage. Ephemeral resources always produce ephemeral values.\\n5:  - **Ephemeral values**: Input variables and outputs can now be defined as ephemeral. Ephemeral values may only be used in certain contexts in Terraform configuration, and are not persisted to the plan or state files.\\n6:     - **`ephemeralasnull` function**: a function takes a value of any type and returns a similar value of the same type with any ephemeral values replaced with non-ephemeral null values and all non-ephemeral values preserved.\\n7: \\n8: BUG FIXES:\\n9: \\n10: - The `secret_suffix` in the `kubernetes` backend now includes validation to prevent errors when the `secret_suffix` ends with a number ([#35666](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35666)).\\n11: - The error message for an invalid default value for an input variable now indicates when the problem is with a nested value in a complex data type. ([#35465](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35465))\\n12: - Sensitive marks could be incorrectly transferred to nested resource values, causing erroneous changes during a plan ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n13: - Allow unknown `error_message` values to pass the core validate step, so variable validation can be completed later during plan\\n14:   ([#35537](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35537))\\n15: - Unencoded slashes within GitHub module source refs were being truncated and incorrectly used as subdirectories in the request path ([#35552](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35552))\\n16: - Terraform refresh-only plans with output only changes are now applyable. ([#35812](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35812))\\n17: - Postconditions referencing `self` with many instances could encounter an error during evaluation ([#35895](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35895))\\n18: - The `plantimestamp()` function would return an invalid date during validation ([#35902](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35902))\\n19: - Updates to resources which were forced to use create_before_destroy could lose that flag in the state temporarily and cause cycles if immediately removed from the configuration ([#35966](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35966))\\n20: - backend/cloud: Prefer KV tags, even when tags are defined as set ([#35937](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35937))\\n21: - Simplify config generation (`plan -generate-config-out`) for string attributes that contain primitive types (e.g. numbers or booleans) ([#35984](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35984))\\n22: - config: `issensitive` could incorrectly assert that an unknown value was not sensitive during plan, but later became sensitive during apply, causing failures where changes did not match the planned result ([#36012](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36012))\\n23: - config: The evaluation of conditional expressions and for expression in HCL could lose marks with certain combinations of unknown values ([#36017](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/36017))\\n24: \\n25: ENHANCEMENTS:\\n26: \\n27: - The `element` function now accepts negative indices ([#35501](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35501))\\n28: - Import block validation has been improved to provide more useful errors and catch more invalid cases during `terraform validate` ([#35543](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35543))\\n29: - Performance enhancements for resource evaluation, especially when large numbers of resource instances are involved ([#35558](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35558))\\n30: - The `plan`, `apply`, and `refresh` commands now produce a deprecated warning when using the `-state` flag. Instead use the `path` attribute within the `local` backend to modify the state file. ([#35660](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35660))\\n31: - backend/cos: Add new auth for Tencent Cloud backend ([#35888](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/pull/35888))\\n32: \\n33: UPGRADE NOTES:\\n34: \\n35: - backend/s3: Removes deprecated attributes for assuming IAM role. Must use the `assume_role` block ([#35721](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35721))\\n36: - backend/s3: The s3 backend now supports S3 native state locking. When used with DynamoDB-based locking, locks will be acquired from both sources. In a future minor release of Terraform the DynamoDB locking mechanism and associated arguments will be deprecated. ([#35661](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35661))\\n37: - `moved`: Moved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. Configurations that reference resources with type names that match top level blocks and keywords from `moved` blocks will need to prepend the `resource.` identifier to these references. ([#35850](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/issues/35850))\\n38: - config: In order to ensure consistency in results from HCL conditional expressions, marks must be combined from all values within the expression to avoid losing mark information. This typically improves accuracy when validating configuration, but users may see sensitive results where they were lost previously.\\n39: \\n40: ## Previous Releases\\n41: \\n42: For information on prior major and minor releases, refer to their changelogs:\\n43: \\n44: - [v1.9](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.9/CHANGELOG.md)\\n45: - [v1.8](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.8/CHANGELOG.md)\\n46: - [v1.7](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.7/CHANGELOG.md)\\n47: - [v1.6](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.6/CHANGELOG.md)\\n48: - [v1.5](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.5/CHANGELOG.md)\\n49: - [v1.4](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.4/CHANGELOG.md)\\n50: - [v1.3](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.3/CHANGELOG.md)\\n51: - [v1.2](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.2/CHANGELOG.md)\\n52: - [v1.1](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.1/CHANGELOG.md)\\n53: - [v1.0](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v1.0/CHANGELOG.md)\\n54: - [v0.15](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.15/CHANGELOG.md)\\n55: - [v0.14](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.14/CHANGELOG.md)\\n56: - [v0.13](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.13/CHANGELOG.md)\\n57: - [v0.12](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.12/CHANGELOG.md)\\n58: - [v0.11 and earlier](https://github.com/hashicorp/terraform/blob/v0.11/CHANGELOG.md)\\n59: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-benchmarks/terraform--24236f4f@e1a7505de5f9af1ffec8078d6baa58426aa7c353/-/blob/CHANGELOG.md%3FL1-100\"}","structuredContent":{"content":"1: ## 1.10.0 (November 27, 2024)\n2: \n3: NEW FEATURES:\n4:  - **Ephemeral resources**: Ephemeral resources are read anew during each phase of Terraform evaluation, and cannot be persisted to state storage. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_018C9DMZaiXc4H7D4ov8jHuf","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_015wrRVs8n5tPfq7uDutLto8","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Terraform v1.9.0 to v1.10.0 Migration Guide\n\n## Overview\n\nTerraform v1.10.0 is a minor release that maintains compatibility with the v1.0 Compatibility Promises. However, there are several important changes that may require updates to your Terraform configuration:\n\n1. **S3 Backend Changes** - Deprecated IAM role assumption attributes have been removed; migration to the `assume_role` block is required\n2. **Moved Blocks Syntax Changes** - Reserved keywords now require explicit `resource.` prefix in moved block references\n3. **Sensitive Value Handling** - Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions; marks are now combined to prevent losing sensitivity information\n4. **Ephemeral Resources and Values** - New feature for handling temporary, non-persistent data\n\nThis guide provides step-by-step migration instructions for each change.\n\n---\n\n## 1. S3 Backend Changes\n\n### 1.1 Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n**What Changed:**\nIn Terraform v1.10.0, several root-level attributes for assuming IAM roles in the S3 backend have been removed. These attributes were deprecated in earlier versions and have now been entirely removed from the codebase.\n\n**Removed Attributes:**\n| Removed Attribute | Replacement |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arns` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n**Why This Change:**\nThe removal consolidates IAM role assumption configuration into a single, well-structured `assume_role` block, improving consistency across backend configuration and making the schema clearer.\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket               = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key                  = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region               = \"us-east-1\"\n    role_arn             = \"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:role/Terraform\"\n    session_name         = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id          = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy   = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_policy_arns = [\"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:policy/MyPolicy\"]\n    assume_role_tags     = {\"Environment\" = \"Production\"}\n    assume_role_transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn            = \"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:role/Terraform\"\n      session_name        = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id         = \"my-external-id\"\n      duration            = 3600                                      # in seconds\n      policy              = jsonencode({...})\n      policy_arns         = [\"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:policy/MyPolicy\"]\n      tags                = {\"Environment\" = \"Production\"}\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Steps:**\n\n1. **Identify affected backend configurations** - Search your Terraform code for any of the removed root-level attributes in S3 backend blocks.\n\n2. **Create or update the `assume_role` block** - Move all role assumption configuration into a single `assume_role` block.\n\n3. **Update attribute names** - Use the replacement names listed in the table above when moving attributes into the block:\n   - `assume_role_duration_seconds` becomes `duration`\n   - `assume_role_policy` becomes `policy`\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` becomes `policy_arns`\n   - `assume_role_tags` becomes `tags`\n   - `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` becomes `transitive_tag_keys`\n   - `role_arn`, `session_name`, and `external_id` remain the same\n\n4. **Test the migration** - Run `terraform init` in affected workspaces to validate the new configuration:\n   ```bash\n   terraform init -reconfigure\n   ```\n\n5. **Verify access** - Ensure that Terraform can still access and lock your state file with the new assume role configuration.\n\n**Common Pitfalls:**\n\n- **Mixing old and new syntax**: Don't use both the old root-level attributes and the new `assume_role` block at the same time. Terraform will fail with an error.\n- **Forgetting to update duration type**: If you were using `assume_role_duration_seconds`, remember it maps to `duration` in the block, and should be specified in seconds (as a number, not a string).\n- **State file access loss**: If your IAM role permissions have changed or if the assume role configuration is incorrect, you may lose access to your state file. Test in a non-production environment first.\n\n**Example Migration with Multiple Roles:**\n\nv1.10.0 also supports multiple `assume_role` values that will be assumed in order:\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Assume this role first\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:role/InitialRole\"\n    }\n\n    # Then assume this role\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:role/FinalRole\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 1.2 S3 Native State Locking (New Optional Feature)\n\n**What Changed:**\nThe S3 backend now supports native S3-based state locking as an opt-in, experimental feature. Previously, only DynamoDB-based locking was available.\n\n**Why This Change:**\nS3 native locking reduces dependencies (no need for separate DynamoDB table) and simplifies state file management for users who prefer to keep everything in S3.\n\n**Enable S3 Native Locking:**\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region       = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile = true  # Enable experimental S3 native locking\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Lock File Details:**\n\n- Lock files are placed in the same S3 location as the state file\n- Lock filename = state filename + `.tflock` extension\n- Example: if state is `prod/terraform.tfstate`, lock file is `prod/terraform.tfstate.tflock`\n\n**Important Permissions:**\n\nWhen enabling S3 native locking, update your S3 bucket policies and IAM policies to include permissions for managing the lock files. You may need to add permissions like:\n\n- `s3:GetObject` and `s3:PutObject` for `.tflock` files\n- `s3:DeleteObject` for releasing locks\n- `s3:ListBucket` to check lock file existence\n\n**Using S3 Locking Alongside DynamoDB:**\n\nWhen both S3 native locking and DynamoDB locking are configured, Terraform will acquire locks from **both sources**. Locks must be successfully acquired from both locations before operations proceed.\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket            = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key               = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region            = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile      = true              # S3 native locking\n    dynamodb_table    = \"terraform-locks\" # DynamoDB locking\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Future Deprecation Notice:**\n\nIn a future minor release of Terraform, DynamoDB-based locking arguments will be deprecated. Plan your migration accordingly:\n\n1. If currently using only DynamoDB locking, you can optionally adopt S3 native locking\n2. If using both, plan a gradual migration away from DynamoDB\n3. Test thoroughly in staging before migrating production state\n\n---\n\n## 2. Moved Blocks Syntax Changes\n\n### 2.1 Conflicting Moved Block References\n\n**What Changed:**\n`moved` blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. If a resource type name matches a reserved keyword (like `local`, `each`, `self`, `data`, `resource`, etc.), you must now prepend `resource.` to explicitly reference it as a resource.\n\n**Why This Change:**\nThis change disambiguates configurations and prevents accidental conflicts with Terraform's language keywords and built-in blocks.\n\n**Affected Reserved Keywords:**\n\nThe following keywords now require the `resource.` prefix if used as resource type names:\n- `data` - used for data sources\n- `local` - used for local values\n- `variable` - used for input variables\n- `output` - used for outputs\n- `resource` - used for resources\n- `each`, `self`, `count` - used in meta-arguments and expressions\n- Other language reserved words\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n\nIf you had a resource type `local` (from a custom provider), the `moved` block would look like:\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = local.example\n  to   = local.renamed\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n\nYou must now explicitly use `resource.` prefix:\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = resource.local.renamed\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Steps:**\n\n1. **Identify conflicting resource types** - Search your codebase for any `moved` blocks that reference resource types matching reserved keywords.\n\n2. **Add `resource.` prefix** - Prepend `resource.` to resource references in `from` and `to` addresses when the resource type matches a reserved keyword.\n\n3. **Validate the configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   ```\n\n4. **Test the moved block** - Ensure the moved block still correctly handles the resource migration:\n   ```bash\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n**Examples:**\n\nExample 1: Moving a custom `local` resource type:\n```hcl\n# Moved block for a custom provider's \"local\" resource type\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_name\n  to   = resource.local.new_name\n}\n```\n\nExample 2: Moving a resource that used a reserved word in older provider versions:\n```hcl\n# If you had a resource type named \"data\" from a custom provider\nmoved {\n  from = resource.data.old_instance\n  to   = resource.data.new_instance\n}\n```\n\nExample 3: Multiple moves with reserved keywords:\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.service.old_id\n  to   = resource.local.service.new_id\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = resource.variable.config\n  to   = resource.variable.renamed_config\n}\n```\n\n**Validation Errors:**\n\nIf you don't add the `resource.` prefix when needed, Terraform will report an error during validation:\n\n```\nError: Conflicting moved block references\n\n  on main.tf line X:\n    X: moved {\n\nMoved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses.\nConfigurations that reference resources with type names matching top level blocks\nand keywords must prepend the \"resource.\" identifier to these references.\n```\n\n**Common Pitfalls:**\n\n- **Only adding prefix to `from`**: Remember to add the prefix to **both** `from` and `to` addresses\n- **Forgetting about custom providers**: If you use custom providers with resource type names matching keywords, all your `moved` blocks need updating\n- **Nested modules**: Check `moved` blocks in all modules and workspaces, not just the root module\n\n---\n\n## 3. Sensitive Value Handling and Mark Propagation\n\n### 3.1 Improved Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions\n\n**What Changed:**\nTerraform v1.10.0 improves how sensitive and other value marks are propagated through conditional expressions and for loops. Previously, marks could be lost in certain combinations of conditional expressions with unknown values. Now, marks are properly combined from all branches to ensure consistency.\n\n**Why This Change:**\nThis change improves accuracy in detecting sensitive values and prevents inconsistent behavior where a value might be marked as sensitive in some code paths but not others.\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n\nIn some cases, sensitive marks could be lost when evaluating conditional expressions, leading to:\n- Sensitive values being unexpectedly exposed in plans\n- Inconsistent plan results between multiple runs\n\nExample of lost marks:\n```hcl\n# In v1.9.0, the sensitive mark could be lost in conditional expressions\nlocals {\n  sensitive_db_password = var.enable_password ? sensitive(var.db_password) : null\n}\n\n# The result might not preserve the sensitive mark in all code paths\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n\nMarks are now properly combined from all branches:\n\n```hcl\n# In v1.10.0, sensitive marks are preserved across all branches\nlocals {\n  sensitive_db_password = var.enable_password ? sensitive(var.db_password) : null\n}\n\n# The result will be marked as sensitive regardless of the condition\n```\n\n**Migration Impact:**\n\nThis change is mostly transparent, but you may notice:\n\n1. **More values marked as sensitive** - If you have configurations where marks were previously lost, those values will now correctly be marked as sensitive.\n\n2. **Plan changes may differ** - If you have existing plans or plan files, re-running `terraform plan` may show more attributes as sensitive than before.\n\n3. **Reduced false positives** - You may see fewer warnings about sensitive values in contexts where they shouldn't appear.\n\n**Using `nonsensitive()` to Override:**\n\nIf you intentionally want to work with sensitive values without the mark, use the `nonsensitive()` function:\n\n```hcl\n# Use nonsensitive() to remove the sensitive mark when appropriate\noutput \"non_secret_id\" {\n  value       = aws_db_instance.example.id\n  sensitive   = false\n  description = \"The ID is not sensitive, even if derived from sensitive values\"\n}\n\n# Or in expressions\nlocals {\n  # Remove sensitivity from a derived value if it's safe\n  db_connection_string = \"${aws_db_instance.example.endpoint}:${nonsensitive(aws_db_instance.example.port)}\"\n}\n```\n\n**Common Scenarios:**\n\nScenario 1: Sensitive passwords in conditional expressions\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"use_provided_password\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # In v1.10.0, this is correctly marked as sensitive\n  password = var.use_provided_password ? var.db_password : random_password.generated.result\n}\n\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value     = local.password\n  sensitive = true  # Explicitly mark as sensitive\n}\n```\n\nScenario 2: Combining sensitive values in for expressions\n```hcl\nvariable \"sensitive_list\" {\n  type      = list(string)\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # All values derived from sensitive_list are marked as sensitive\n  uppercase_list = [for item in var.sensitive_list : upper(item)]\n}\n```\n\n**Testing the Change:**\n\nTo verify your configuration handles marks correctly:\n\n1. Run `terraform plan` and look for sensitive value warnings in affected outputs\n2. Compare behavior before and after migration\n3. Use `terraform console` to test expressions:\n   ```bash\n   terraform console\n   # Test mark propagation\n   > var.db_password\n   sensitive(\"mypassword\")\n   > var.enable ? var.db_password : null\n   sensitive(value_depends_on_condition)\n   ```\n\n**Potential Issues and Fixes:**\n\nIssue: \"Conflicting marks in output\"\n```\nError: Output contains sensitive value, but is not marked sensitive\n  The output value refers to a sensitive value but is not marked sensitive itself.\n```\n\nFix: Explicitly mark outputs as sensitive:\n```hcl\noutput \"database_password\" {\n  value     = var.db_password\n  sensitive = true\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Ephemeral Resources and Values (New Feature)\n\n### 4.1 Introduction to Ephemeral Values\n\n**What Is New:**\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces ephemeral resources and ephemeral variables/outputs. These are values that:\n- Are available during Terraform operations (plan, apply, etc.)\n- Are **never written to state or plan files**\n- Are not persisted between operations\n- Are only available in specific contexts\n\n**Why This Feature:**\nEphemeral values are designed for handling temporary, short-lived credentials and sensitive data that should never be persisted. This is especially useful for:\n- Short-lived authentication tokens (15-60 minutes)\n- Session credentials\n- Temporary API keys\n- Time-sensitive security credentials\n\n### 4.2 Ephemeral Input Variables\n\n**What Changed:**\nInput variables can now be marked as `ephemeral = true`, making them unavailable for persistence in state or plan files.\n\n**Use Case:**\nPassing temporary credentials to providers or resources without storing them:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"temporary_aws_credentials\" {\n  type = object({\n    access_key = string\n    secret_key = string\n    session_token = string\n    expiration_time = number\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"Temporary AWS credentials from STS assume role\"\n}\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n\n- Ephemeral variables can only be referenced in specific contexts:\n  - Other ephemeral variables\n  - Local values\n  - Ephemeral resources\n  - Ephemeral outputs\n  - Provider configurations\n  - Provisioner and connection blocks\n\n- If a non-ephemeral expression references an ephemeral variable, Terraform will error:\n  ```\n  Error: Cannot use ephemeral variable in non-ephemeral context\n  ```\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n\nNo ephemeral variables available. All variables were persistent.\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n\nMark sensitive, temporary variables as ephemeral:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"aws_session_credentials\" {\n  type = object({\n    access_key    = string\n    secret_key    = string\n    session_token = string\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# Use in provider configuration (ephemeral context)\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = var.aws_session_credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = var.aws_session_credentials.secret_key\n  token      = var.aws_session_credentials.session_token\n}\n\n# Use in local values (valid ephemeral context)\nlocals {\n  session_expiry = var.aws_session_credentials.expiration_time\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Guidance:**\n\n1. **Identify credential variables** - Find all input variables that contain temporary credentials or short-lived tokens\n2. **Mark as ephemeral** - Add `ephemeral = true` to the variable declaration\n3. **Test credential passing** - Ensure credentials are still passed correctly to providers\n4. **Verify no state leakage** - Run `terraform apply` and verify that `terraform.tfstate` contains no credential data\n\n### 4.3 Ephemeral Resources\n\n**What Is New:**\nCustom providers can now implement ephemeral resources using `ephemeral \"provider_type\" \"resource_name\"` syntax. These resources are read anew during each phase of evaluation and never persisted.\n\n**Use Case:**\nProviders implementing ephemeral resources for:\n- Fetching temporary credentials (e.g., AssumeRole tokens)\n- Generating one-time passwords\n- Reading time-sensitive data\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```hcl\nephemeral \"aws_sts_assume_role\" \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  role_arn         = aws_iam_role.terraform.arn\n  session_name     = \"terraform-ephemeral-session\"\n  duration_seconds = 3600\n}\n```\n\n**Valid References:**\n\nEphemeral resources can only be referenced in:\n- Other ephemeral resources\n- Local values\n- Ephemeral variables\n- Ephemeral outputs\n- Provider configurations\n- Provisioner and connection blocks\n\n**Example - Using Ephemeral Resources:**\n\n```hcl\n# Fetch temporary credentials ephemerally\nephemeral \"aws_sts_assume_role\" \"terraform_role\" {\n  role_arn     = var.terraform_role_arn\n  session_name = \"terraform-operation\"\n}\n\n# Use in local value (ephemeral)\nlocals {\n  temporary_credentials = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform_role.credentials\n}\n\n# Use in provider (ephemeral context)\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform_role.credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform_role.credentials.secret_key\n  token      = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform_role.credentials.session_token\n}\n```\n\n**Important Note:**\nEphemeral resources are in **public beta** in v1.10.0. Provider support varies. Check your provider documentation to see if ephemeral resources are available.\n\n### 4.4 Ephemeral Outputs\n\n**What Is New:**\nOutputs can be marked as `ephemeral = true`, preventing them from being written to state or plan files.\n\n**Use Case:**\nPassing ephemeral values from child modules to parents without persisting them.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```hcl\noutput \"temporary_session_token\" {\n  value     = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.credentials.session_token\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"Temporary session token from STS\"\n}\n```\n\n**Characteristics:**\n\n- Can only output ephemeral values from ephemeral resources or variables\n- The output value itself is not persisted to state or plan\n- Can be referenced by parent modules in ephemeral contexts\n\n**Example Configuration:**\n\n```hcl\n# Module: credentials/main.tf\nephemeral \"aws_sts_assume_role\" \"assume\" {\n  role_arn     = var.role_arn\n  session_name = \"terraform\"\n}\n\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value = {\n    access_key    = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.assume.credentials.access_key\n    secret_key    = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.assume.credentials.secret_key\n    session_token = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.assume.credentials.session_token\n  }\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# Root module: main.tf\nmodule \"credentials\" {\n  source = \"./credentials\"\n  role_arn = aws_iam_role.terraform.arn\n}\n\n# Use ephemeral output in provider (ephemeral context)\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = module.credentials.temporary_credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = module.credentials.temporary_credentials.secret_key\n  token      = module.credentials.temporary_credentials.session_token\n}\n```\n\n### 4.5 The `ephemeralasnull()` Function\n\n**What Is New:**\nThe `ephemeralasnull()` function replaces all ephemeral values in a value with `null`, while preserving non-ephemeral values.\n\n**Use Case:**\nConverting ephemeral values to non-ephemeral when you need to serialize or export configuration.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```hcl\nephemeralasnull(value)\n```\n\n**Example:**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"sensitive_config\" {\n  type = object({\n    api_key = string\n    timeout = number\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# Replace the ephemeral api_key with null\nlocals {\n  non_ephemeral_config = ephemeralasnull(var.sensitive_config)\n  # Result: { api_key = null, timeout = 30 }\n}\n```\n\n**Common Use:**\n\nMaking data serializable while preserving structure:\n\n```hcl\noutput \"config_for_export\" {\n  value     = ephemeralasnull(local.mixed_config)\n  sensitive = false\n  description = \"Configuration without ephemeral values, safe to export\"\n}\n```\n\n### 4.6 Migration Guidance for Ephemeral Resources/Values\n\n**Step-by-Step Migration:**\n\n1. **Audit current credential handling** - Identify where you're currently storing credentials or sensitive data\n\n2. **Identify short-lived credentials** - Determine which credentials are temporary (session tokens, STS assume role, etc.)\n\n3. **Check provider support** - Verify if your providers support ephemeral resources:\n   - AWS provider may support ephemeral STS operations\n   - Check provider documentation\n\n4. **Plan migration path**:\n   - Phase 1: Continue using existing provider configuration with environment variables or external tools\n   - Phase 2: Migrate to ephemeral variables if using third-party credential sources\n   - Phase 3: Adopt ephemeral resources when provider support is available\n\n5. **Test in non-production environment**:\n   ```bash\n   # Test that credentials are not persisted to state\n   terraform plan\n   grep -i \"credential\\|token\\|secret\" terraform.tfstate\n   # Should find no sensitive credentials\n   ```\n\n6. **Validate state file privacy**:\n   ```bash\n   # Ensure no credentials are in state after migration\n   terraform state pull | jq . | grep -i \"access_key\\|secret\"\n   ```\n\n**Example Migration - From Sensitive Variables to Ephemeral:**\n\nBefore (v1.9.0):\n```hcl\nvariable \"aws_access_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  description = \"AWS access key (not ideal - will be in state)\"\n}\n\nvariable \"aws_secret_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  description = \"AWS secret key (not ideal - will be in state)\"\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = var.aws_access_key\n  secret_key = var.aws_secret_key\n}\n```\n\nAfter (v1.10.0):\n```hcl\n# Option 1: Using ephemeral variables with STS assume role\nvariable \"assume_role_arn\" {\n  type        = string\n  description = \"ARN of role to assume\"\n}\n\nephemeral \"aws_sts_assume_role\" \"terraform\" {\n  role_arn     = var.assume_role_arn\n  session_name = \"terraform-plan\"\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform.credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform.credentials.secret_key\n  token      = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform.credentials.session_token\n}\n\n# Option 2: Using ephemeral variable (for pre-obtained temporary credentials)\nvariable \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  type = object({\n    access_key    = string\n    secret_key    = string\n    session_token = string\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"Temporary credentials from external source (e.g., AWS STS, vault, etc.)\"\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = var.temporary_credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = var.temporary_credentials.secret_key\n  token      = var.temporary_credentials.session_token\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Testing Your Migration\n\n### 5.1 Pre-Migration Checklist\n\nBefore upgrading to v1.10.0:\n\n- [ ] Back up your current state file\n- [ ] Review all S3 backend configurations for deprecated attributes\n- [ ] Identify all `moved` blocks using reserved keyword resource types\n- [ ] Document current credential handling approach\n- [ ] Test in a non-production workspace first\n\n### 5.2 Migration Testing Steps\n\n1. **Test S3 Backend Migration:**\n   ```bash\n   # With v1.10.0, reconfigure backend\n   terraform init -reconfigure\n\n   # Verify state is accessible\n   terraform state list\n\n   # Check lock file was created (if using use_lockfile = true)\n   aws s3 ls s3://my-bucket/path/ | grep tflock\n   ```\n\n2. **Validate Moved Blocks:**\n   ```bash\n   # Run validation to catch moved block errors\n   terraform validate\n\n   # Plan to ensure moves work correctly\n   terraform plan -out=tfplan\n\n   # Verify no resources are being recreated\n   grep -i \"will be destroyed\\|will be created\" tfplan\n   ```\n\n3. **Test Sensitive Value Handling:**\n   ```bash\n   # Plan and check for unexpected sensitive values\n   terraform plan -json | jq '.resource_changes[] | select(.change.sensitive != null)'\n\n   # Verify state doesn't contain credentials\n   terraform state pull | jq . | grep -E \"(password|secret|key|token)\" | wc -l\n   ```\n\n4. **Test Ephemeral Values (if used):**\n   ```bash\n   # Plan should succeed without persisting ephemeral values\n   terraform plan\n\n   # Verify state after apply\n   terraform apply\n   terraform state show <resource> | grep -i \"ephemeral\"\n   # Should show no ephemeral data\n   ```\n\n### 5.3 Rollback Procedure\n\nIf you encounter issues after upgrading:\n\n1. **Stop using v1.10.0:**\n   ```bash\n   # Switch back to v1.9.0\n   terraform version  # Verify downgrade\n   ```\n\n2. **Revert configuration changes:**\n   ```bash\n   # Restore from git or backup\n   git checkout HEAD -- .\n   ```\n\n3. **Reconfigure backend if needed:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform init -reconfigure\n   ```\n\n4. **Verify state is accessible:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform state list\n   ```\n\nFor S3 backend, if you enabled `use_lockfile = true`:\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    # Remove or set to false\n    # use_lockfile = false\n  }\n}\n\n# Then reconfigure\nterraform init -reconfigure\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Summary of Breaking Changes\n\n| Change | Impact | Required Action |\n|--------|--------|-----------------|\n| S3 backend deprecated IAM attributes removed | All S3 backends with IAM role assumption must be updated | Migrate to `assume_role` block |\n| Moved blocks require `resource.` prefix for reserved keywords | Any `moved` blocks referencing resources with reserved keyword names | Add `resource.` prefix to addresses |\n| Sensitive marks now propagate in conditional expressions | May see more values marked as sensitive | Review plan output; use `nonsensitive()` if needed |\n| Ephemeral resources/values introduced | New feature, optional adoption | Plan migration for temporary credentials |\n\n---\n\n## 7. However, there are several important changes that may require updates to your Terraform configuration:\n\n1. **S3 Backend Changes** - Deprecated IAM role assumption attributes have been removed; migration to the `assume_role` block is required\n2. **Moved Blocks Syntax Changes** - Reserved keywords now require explicit `resource.` prefix in moved block references\n3. **Sensitive Value Handling** - Improved mark propagation in conditional expressions; marks are now combined to prevent losing sensitivity information\n4. **Ephemeral Resources and Values** - New feature for handling temporary, non-persistent data\n\nThis guide provides step-by-step migration instructions for each change.\n\n---\n\n## 1. S3 Backend Changes\n\n### 1.1 Removal of Deprecated IAM Role Assumption Attributes\n\n**What Changed:**\nIn Terraform v1.10.0, several root-level attributes for assuming IAM roles in the S3 backend have been removed. These attributes were deprecated in earlier versions and have now been entirely removed from the codebase.\n\n**Removed Attributes:**\n| Removed Attribute | Replacement |\n|---|---|\n| `role_arn` | `assume_role.role_arn` |\n| `session_name` | `assume_role.session_name` |\n| `external_id` | `assume_role.external_id` |\n| `assume_role_duration_seconds` | `assume_role.duration` |\n| `assume_role_policy` | `assume_role.policy` |\n| `assume_role_policy_arns` | `assume_role.policy_arns` |\n| `assume_role_tags` | `assume_role.tags` |\n| `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` | `assume_role.transitive_tag_keys` |\n\n**Why This Change:**\nThe removal consolidates IAM role assumption configuration into a single, well-structured `assume_role` block, improving consistency across backend configuration and making the schema clearer.\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket               = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key                  = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region               = \"us-east-1\"\n    role_arn             = \"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:role/Terraform\"\n    session_name         = \"terraform-session\"\n    external_id          = \"my-external-id\"\n    assume_role_duration_seconds = 3600\n    assume_role_policy   = jsonencode({...})\n    assume_role_policy_arns = [\"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:policy/MyPolicy\"]\n    assume_role_tags     = {\"Environment\" = \"Production\"}\n    assume_role_transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key    = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn            = \"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:role/Terraform\"\n      session_name        = \"terraform-session\"\n      external_id         = \"my-external-id\"\n      duration            = 3600                                      # in seconds\n      policy              = jsonencode({...})\n      policy_arns         = [\"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:policy/MyPolicy\"]\n      tags                = {\"Environment\" = \"Production\"}\n      transitive_tag_keys = [\"Environment\"]\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Steps:**\n\n1. **Identify affected backend configurations** - Search your Terraform code for any of the removed root-level attributes in S3 backend blocks.\n\n2. **Create or update the `assume_role` block** - Move all role assumption configuration into a single `assume_role` block.\n\n3. **Update attribute names** - Use the replacement names listed in the table above when moving attributes into the block:\n   - `assume_role_duration_seconds` becomes `duration`\n   - `assume_role_policy` becomes `policy`\n   - `assume_role_policy_arns` becomes `policy_arns`\n   - `assume_role_tags` becomes `tags`\n   - `assume_role_transitive_tag_keys` becomes `transitive_tag_keys`\n   - `role_arn`, `session_name`, and `external_id` remain the same\n\n4. **Test the migration** - Run `terraform init` in affected workspaces to validate the new configuration:\n   ```bash\n   terraform init -reconfigure\n   ```\n\n5. **Verify access** - Ensure that Terraform can still access and lock your state file with the new assume role configuration.\n\n**Common Pitfalls:**\n\n- **Mixing old and new syntax**: Don't use both the old root-level attributes and the new `assume_role` block at the same time. Terraform will fail with an error.\n- **Forgetting to update duration type**: If you were using `assume_role_duration_seconds`, remember it maps to `duration` in the block, and should be specified in seconds (as a number, not a string).\n- **State file access loss**: If your IAM role permissions have changed or if the assume role configuration is incorrect, you may lose access to your state file. Test in a non-production environment first.\n\n**Example Migration with Multiple Roles:**\n\nv1.10.0 also supports multiple `assume_role` values that will be assumed in order:\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    region = \"us-east-1\"\n\n    # Assume this role first\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:role/InitialRole\"\n    }\n\n    # Then assume this role\n    assume_role {\n      role_arn = \"arn:aws:iam::PRODUCTION-ACCOUNT-ID:role/FinalRole\"\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 1.2 S3 Native State Locking (New Optional Feature)\n\n**What Changed:**\nThe S3 backend now supports native S3-based state locking as an opt-in, experimental feature. Previously, only DynamoDB-based locking was available.\n\n**Why This Change:**\nS3 native locking reduces dependencies (no need for separate DynamoDB table) and simplifies state file management for users who prefer to keep everything in S3.\n\n**Enable S3 Native Locking:**\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket       = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key          = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region       = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile = true  # Enable experimental S3 native locking\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Lock File Details:**\n\n- Lock files are placed in the same S3 location as the state file\n- Lock filename = state filename + `.tflock` extension\n- Example: if state is `prod/terraform.tfstate`, lock file is `prod/terraform.tfstate.tflock`\n\n**Important Permissions:**\n\nWhen enabling S3 native locking, update your S3 bucket policies and IAM policies to include permissions for managing the lock files. You may need to add permissions like:\n\n- `s3:GetObject` and `s3:PutObject` for `.tflock` files\n- `s3:DeleteObject` for releasing locks\n- `s3:ListBucket` to check lock file existence\n\n**Using S3 Locking Alongside DynamoDB:**\n\nWhen both S3 native locking and DynamoDB locking are configured, Terraform will acquire locks from **both sources**. Locks must be successfully acquired from both locations before operations proceed.\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    bucket            = \"my-terraform-state\"\n    key               = \"prod/terraform.tfstate\"\n    region            = \"us-east-1\"\n    use_lockfile      = true              # S3 native locking\n    dynamodb_table    = \"terraform-locks\" # DynamoDB locking\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**Future Deprecation Notice:**\n\nIn a future minor release of Terraform, DynamoDB-based locking arguments will be deprecated. Plan your migration accordingly:\n\n1. If currently using only DynamoDB locking, you can optionally adopt S3 native locking\n2. If using both, plan a gradual migration away from DynamoDB\n3. Test thoroughly in staging before migrating production state\n\n---\n\n## 2. Moved Blocks Syntax Changes\n\n### 2.1 Conflicting Moved Block References\n\n**What Changed:**\n`moved` blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses. If a resource type name matches a reserved keyword (like `local`, `each`, `self`, `data`, `resource`, etc.), you must now prepend `resource.` to explicitly reference it as a resource.\n\n**Why This Change:**\nThis change disambiguates configurations and prevents accidental conflicts with Terraform's language keywords and built-in blocks.\n\n**Affected Reserved Keywords:**\n\nThe following keywords now require the `resource.` prefix if used as resource type names:\n- `data` - used for data sources\n- `local` - used for local values\n- `variable` - used for input variables\n- `output` - used for outputs\n- `resource` - used for resources\n- `each`, `self`, `count` - used in meta-arguments and expressions\n- Other language reserved words\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n\nIf you had a resource type `local` (from a custom provider), the `moved` block would look like:\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = local.example\n  to   = local.renamed\n}\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n\nYou must now explicitly use `resource.` prefix:\n\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.example\n  to   = resource.local.renamed\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Steps:**\n\n1. **Identify conflicting resource types** - Search your codebase for any `moved` blocks that reference resource types matching reserved keywords.\n\n2. **Add `resource.` prefix** - Prepend `resource.` to resource references in `from` and `to` addresses when the resource type matches a reserved keyword.\n\n3. **Validate the configuration:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform validate\n   ```\n\n4. **Test the moved block** - Ensure the moved block still correctly handles the resource migration:\n   ```bash\n   terraform plan\n   ```\n\n**Examples:**\n\nExample 1: Moving a custom `local` resource type:\n```hcl\n# Moved block for a custom provider's \"local\" resource type\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.old_name\n  to   = resource.local.new_name\n}\n```\n\nExample 2: Moving a resource that used a reserved word in older provider versions:\n```hcl\n# If you had a resource type named \"data\" from a custom provider\nmoved {\n  from = resource.data.old_instance\n  to   = resource.data.new_instance\n}\n```\n\nExample 3: Multiple moves with reserved keywords:\n```hcl\nmoved {\n  from = resource.local.service.old_id\n  to   = resource.local.service.new_id\n}\n\nmoved {\n  from = resource.variable.config\n  to   = resource.variable.renamed_config\n}\n```\n\n**Validation Errors:**\n\nIf you don't add the `resource.` prefix when needed, Terraform will report an error during validation:\n\n```\nError: Conflicting moved block references\n\n  on main.tf line X:\n    X: moved {\n\nMoved blocks now respect reserved keywords when parsing resource addresses.\nConfigurations that reference resources with type names matching top level blocks\nand keywords must prepend the \"resource.\" identifier to these references.\n```\n\n**Common Pitfalls:**\n\n- **Only adding prefix to `from`**: Remember to add the prefix to **both** `from` and `to` addresses\n- **Forgetting about custom providers**: If you use custom providers with resource type names matching keywords, all your `moved` blocks need updating\n- **Nested modules**: Check `moved` blocks in all modules and workspaces, not just the root module\n\n---\n\n## 3. Sensitive Value Handling and Mark Propagation\n\n### 3.1 Improved Mark Propagation in Conditional Expressions\n\n**What Changed:**\nTerraform v1.10.0 improves how sensitive and other value marks are propagated through conditional expressions and for loops. Previously, marks could be lost in certain combinations of conditional expressions with unknown values. Now, marks are properly combined from all branches to ensure consistency.\n\n**Why This Change:**\nThis change improves accuracy in detecting sensitive values and prevents inconsistent behavior where a value might be marked as sensitive in some code paths but not others.\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n\nIn some cases, sensitive marks could be lost when evaluating conditional expressions, leading to:\n- Sensitive values being unexpectedly exposed in plans\n- Inconsistent plan results between multiple runs\n\nExample of lost marks:\n```hcl\n# In v1.9.0, the sensitive mark could be lost in conditional expressions\nlocals {\n  sensitive_db_password = var.enable_password ? sensitive(var.db_password) : null\n}\n\n# The result might not preserve the sensitive mark in all code paths\n```\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n\nMarks are now properly combined from all branches:\n\n```hcl\n# In v1.10.0, sensitive marks are preserved across all branches\nlocals {\n  sensitive_db_password = var.enable_password ? sensitive(var.db_password) : null\n}\n\n# The result will be marked as sensitive regardless of the condition\n```\n\n**Migration Impact:**\n\nThis change is mostly transparent, but you may notice:\n\n1. **More values marked as sensitive** - If you have configurations where marks were previously lost, those values will now correctly be marked as sensitive.\n\n2. **Plan changes may differ** - If you have existing plans or plan files, re-running `terraform plan` may show more attributes as sensitive than before.\n\n3. **Reduced false positives** - You may see fewer warnings about sensitive values in contexts where they shouldn't appear.\n\n**Using `nonsensitive()` to Override:**\n\nIf you intentionally want to work with sensitive values without the mark, use the `nonsensitive()` function:\n\n```hcl\n# Use nonsensitive() to remove the sensitive mark when appropriate\noutput \"non_secret_id\" {\n  value       = aws_db_instance.example.id\n  sensitive   = false\n  description = \"The ID is not sensitive, even if derived from sensitive values\"\n}\n\n# Or in expressions\nlocals {\n  # Remove sensitivity from a derived value if it's safe\n  db_connection_string = \"${aws_db_instance.example.endpoint}:${nonsensitive(aws_db_instance.example.port)}\"\n}\n```\n\n**Common Scenarios:**\n\nScenario 1: Sensitive passwords in conditional expressions\n```hcl\nvariable \"db_password\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nvariable \"use_provided_password\" {\n  type    = bool\n  default = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # In v1.10.0, this is correctly marked as sensitive\n  password = var.use_provided_password ? var.db_password : random_password.generated.result\n}\n\noutput \"db_password\" {\n  value     = local.password\n  sensitive = true  # Explicitly mark as sensitive\n}\n```\n\nScenario 2: Combining sensitive values in for expressions\n```hcl\nvariable \"sensitive_list\" {\n  type      = list(string)\n  sensitive = true\n}\n\nlocals {\n  # All values derived from sensitive_list are marked as sensitive\n  uppercase_list = [for item in var.sensitive_list : upper(item)]\n}\n```\n\n**Testing the Change:**\n\nTo verify your configuration handles marks correctly:\n\n1. Run `terraform plan` and look for sensitive value warnings in affected outputs\n2. Compare behavior before and after migration\n3. Use `terraform console` to test expressions:\n   ```bash\n   terraform console\n   # Test mark propagation\n   > var.db_password\n   sensitive(\"mypassword\")\n   > var.enable ? var.db_password : null\n   sensitive(value_depends_on_condition)\n   ```\n\n**Potential Issues and Fixes:**\n\nIssue: \"Conflicting marks in output\"\n```\nError: Output contains sensitive value, but is not marked sensitive\n  The output value refers to a sensitive value but is not marked sensitive itself.\n```\n\nFix: Explicitly mark outputs as sensitive:\n```hcl\noutput \"database_password\" {\n  value     = var.db_password\n  sensitive = true\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Ephemeral Resources and Values (New Feature)\n\n### 4.1 Introduction to Ephemeral Values\n\n**What Is New:**\nTerraform v1.10.0 introduces ephemeral resources and ephemeral variables/outputs. These are values that:\n- Are available during Terraform operations (plan, apply, etc.)\n- Are **never written to state or plan files**\n- Are not persisted between operations\n- Are only available in specific contexts\n\n**Why This Feature:**\nEphemeral values are designed for handling temporary, short-lived credentials and sensitive data that should never be persisted. This is especially useful for:\n- Short-lived authentication tokens (15-60 minutes)\n- Session credentials\n- Temporary API keys\n- Time-sensitive security credentials\n\n### 4.2 Ephemeral Input Variables\n\n**What Changed:**\nInput variables can now be marked as `ephemeral = true`, making them unavailable for persistence in state or plan files.\n\n**Use Case:**\nPassing temporary credentials to providers or resources without storing them:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"temporary_aws_credentials\" {\n  type = object({\n    access_key = string\n    secret_key = string\n    session_token = string\n    expiration_time = number\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"Temporary AWS credentials from STS assume role\"\n}\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n\n- Ephemeral variables can only be referenced in specific contexts:\n  - Other ephemeral variables\n  - Local values\n  - Ephemeral resources\n  - Ephemeral outputs\n  - Provider configurations\n  - Provisioner and connection blocks\n\n- If a non-ephemeral expression references an ephemeral variable, Terraform will error:\n  ```\n  Error: Cannot use ephemeral variable in non-ephemeral context\n  ```\n\n**Before (v1.9.0):**\n\nNo ephemeral variables available. All variables were persistent.\n\n**After (v1.10.0):**\n\nMark sensitive, temporary variables as ephemeral:\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"aws_session_credentials\" {\n  type = object({\n    access_key    = string\n    secret_key    = string\n    session_token = string\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# Use in provider configuration (ephemeral context)\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = var.aws_session_credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = var.aws_session_credentials.secret_key\n  token      = var.aws_session_credentials.session_token\n}\n\n# Use in local values (valid ephemeral context)\nlocals {\n  session_expiry = var.aws_session_credentials.expiration_time\n}\n```\n\n**Migration Guidance:**\n\n1. **Identify credential variables** - Find all input variables that contain temporary credentials or short-lived tokens\n2. **Mark as ephemeral** - Add `ephemeral = true` to the variable declaration\n3. **Test credential passing** - Ensure credentials are still passed correctly to providers\n4. **Verify no state leakage** - Run `terraform apply` and verify that `terraform.tfstate` contains no credential data\n\n### 4.3 Ephemeral Resources\n\n**What Is New:**\nCustom providers can now implement ephemeral resources using `ephemeral \"provider_type\" \"resource_name\"` syntax. These resources are read anew during each phase of evaluation and never persisted.\n\n**Use Case:**\nProviders implementing ephemeral resources for:\n- Fetching temporary credentials (e.g., AssumeRole tokens)\n- Generating one-time passwords\n- Reading time-sensitive data\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```hcl\nephemeral \"aws_sts_assume_role\" \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  role_arn         = aws_iam_role.terraform.arn\n  session_name     = \"terraform-ephemeral-session\"\n  duration_seconds = 3600\n}\n```\n\n**Valid References:**\n\nEphemeral resources can only be referenced in:\n- Other ephemeral resources\n- Local values\n- Ephemeral variables\n- Ephemeral outputs\n- Provider configurations\n- Provisioner and connection blocks\n\n**Example - Using Ephemeral Resources:**\n\n```hcl\n# Fetch temporary credentials ephemerally\nephemeral \"aws_sts_assume_role\" \"terraform_role\" {\n  role_arn     = var.terraform_role_arn\n  session_name = \"terraform-operation\"\n}\n\n# Use in local value (ephemeral)\nlocals {\n  temporary_credentials = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform_role.credentials\n}\n\n# Use in provider (ephemeral context)\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform_role.credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform_role.credentials.secret_key\n  token      = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform_role.credentials.session_token\n}\n```\n\n**Important Note:**\nEphemeral resources are in **public beta** in v1.10.0. Provider support varies. Check your provider documentation to see if ephemeral resources are available.\n\n### 4.4 Ephemeral Outputs\n\n**What Is New:**\nOutputs can be marked as `ephemeral = true`, preventing them from being written to state or plan files.\n\n**Use Case:**\nPassing ephemeral values from child modules to parents without persisting them.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```hcl\noutput \"temporary_session_token\" {\n  value     = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.credentials.session_token\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"Temporary session token from STS\"\n}\n```\n\n**Characteristics:**\n\n- Can only output ephemeral values from ephemeral resources or variables\n- The output value itself is not persisted to state or plan\n- Can be referenced by parent modules in ephemeral contexts\n\n**Example Configuration:**\n\n```hcl\n# Module: credentials/main.tf\nephemeral \"aws_sts_assume_role\" \"assume\" {\n  role_arn     = var.role_arn\n  session_name = \"terraform\"\n}\n\noutput \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  value = {\n    access_key    = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.assume.credentials.access_key\n    secret_key    = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.assume.credentials.secret_key\n    session_token = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.assume.credentials.session_token\n  }\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# Root module: main.tf\nmodule \"credentials\" {\n  source = \"./credentials\"\n  role_arn = aws_iam_role.terraform.arn\n}\n\n# Use ephemeral output in provider (ephemeral context)\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = module.credentials.temporary_credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = module.credentials.temporary_credentials.secret_key\n  token      = module.credentials.temporary_credentials.session_token\n}\n```\n\n### 4.5 The `ephemeralasnull()` Function\n\n**What Is New:**\nThe `ephemeralasnull()` function replaces all ephemeral values in a value with `null`, while preserving non-ephemeral values.\n\n**Use Case:**\nConverting ephemeral values to non-ephemeral when you need to serialize or export configuration.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```hcl\nephemeralasnull(value)\n```\n\n**Example:**\n\n```hcl\nvariable \"sensitive_config\" {\n  type = object({\n    api_key = string\n    timeout = number\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n}\n\n# Replace the ephemeral api_key with null\nlocals {\n  non_ephemeral_config = ephemeralasnull(var.sensitive_config)\n  # Result: { api_key = null, timeout = 30 }\n}\n```\n\n**Common Use:**\n\nMaking data serializable while preserving structure:\n\n```hcl\noutput \"config_for_export\" {\n  value     = ephemeralasnull(local.mixed_config)\n  sensitive = false\n  description = \"Configuration without ephemeral values, safe to export\"\n}\n```\n\n### 4.6 Migration Guidance for Ephemeral Resources/Values\n\n**Step-by-Step Migration:**\n\n1. **Audit current credential handling** - Identify where you're currently storing credentials or sensitive data\n\n2. **Identify short-lived credentials** - Determine which credentials are temporary (session tokens, STS assume role, etc.)\n\n3. **Check provider support** - Verify if your providers support ephemeral resources:\n   - AWS provider may support ephemeral STS operations\n   - Check provider documentation\n\n4. **Plan migration path**:\n   - Phase 1: Continue using existing provider configuration with environment variables or external tools\n   - Phase 2: Migrate to ephemeral variables if using third-party credential sources\n   - Phase 3: Adopt ephemeral resources when provider support is available\n\n5. **Test in non-production environment**:\n   ```bash\n   # Test that credentials are not persisted to state\n   terraform plan\n   grep -i \"credential\\|token\\|secret\" terraform.tfstate\n   # Should find no sensitive credentials\n   ```\n\n6. **Validate state file privacy**:\n   ```bash\n   # Ensure no credentials are in state after migration\n   terraform state pull | jq . | grep -i \"access_key\\|secret\"\n   ```\n\n**Example Migration - From Sensitive Variables to Ephemeral:**\n\nBefore (v1.9.0):\n```hcl\nvariable \"aws_access_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  description = \"AWS access key (not ideal - will be in state)\"\n}\n\nvariable \"aws_secret_key\" {\n  type      = string\n  sensitive = true\n  description = \"AWS secret key (not ideal - will be in state)\"\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = var.aws_access_key\n  secret_key = var.aws_secret_key\n}\n```\n\nAfter (v1.10.0):\n```hcl\n# Option 1: Using ephemeral variables with STS assume role\nvariable \"assume_role_arn\" {\n  type        = string\n  description = \"ARN of role to assume\"\n}\n\nephemeral \"aws_sts_assume_role\" \"terraform\" {\n  role_arn     = var.assume_role_arn\n  session_name = \"terraform-plan\"\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform.credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform.credentials.secret_key\n  token      = ephemeral.aws_sts_assume_role.terraform.credentials.session_token\n}\n\n# Option 2: Using ephemeral variable (for pre-obtained temporary credentials)\nvariable \"temporary_credentials\" {\n  type = object({\n    access_key    = string\n    secret_key    = string\n    session_token = string\n  })\n  ephemeral = true\n  description = \"Temporary credentials from external source (e.g., AWS STS, vault, etc.)\"\n}\n\nprovider \"aws\" {\n  region     = var.region\n  access_key = var.temporary_credentials.access_key\n  secret_key = var.temporary_credentials.secret_key\n  token      = var.temporary_credentials.session_token\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Testing Your Migration\n\n### 5.1 Pre-Migration Checklist\n\nBefore upgrading to v1.10.0:\n\n- [ ] Back up your current state file\n- [ ] Review all S3 backend configurations for deprecated attributes\n- [ ] Identify all `moved` blocks using reserved keyword resource types\n- [ ] Document current credential handling approach\n- [ ] Test in a non-production workspace first\n\n### 5.2 Migration Testing Steps\n\n1. **Test S3 Backend Migration:**\n   ```bash\n   # With v1.10.0, reconfigure backend\n   terraform init -reconfigure\n\n   # Verify state is accessible\n   terraform state list\n\n   # Check lock file was created (if using use_lockfile = true)\n   aws s3 ls s3://my-bucket/path/ | grep tflock\n   ```\n\n2. **Validate Moved Blocks:**\n   ```bash\n   # Run validation to catch moved block errors\n   terraform validate\n\n   # Plan to ensure moves work correctly\n   terraform plan -out=tfplan\n\n   # Verify no resources are being recreated\n   grep -i \"will be destroyed\\|will be created\" tfplan\n   ```\n\n3. **Test Sensitive Value Handling:**\n   ```bash\n   # Plan and check for unexpected sensitive values\n   terraform plan -json | jq '.resource_changes[] | select(.change.sensitive != null)'\n\n   # Verify state doesn't contain credentials\n   terraform state pull | jq . | grep -E \"(password|secret|key|token)\" | wc -l\n   ```\n\n4. **Test Ephemeral Values (if used):**\n   ```bash\n   # Plan should succeed without persisting ephemeral values\n   terraform plan\n\n   # Verify state after apply\n   terraform apply\n   terraform state show <resource> | grep -i \"ephemeral\"\n   # Should show no ephemeral data\n   ```\n\n### 5.3 Rollback Procedure\n\nIf you encounter issues after upgrading:\n\n1. **Stop using v1.10.0:**\n   ```bash\n   # Switch back to v1.9.0\n   terraform version  # Verify downgrade\n   ```\n\n2. **Revert configuration changes:**\n   ```bash\n   # Restore from git or backup\n   git checkout HEAD -- .\n   ```\n\n3. **Reconfigure backend if needed:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform init -reconfigure\n   ```\n\n4. **Verify state is accessible:**\n   ```bash\n   terraform state list\n   ```\n\nFor S3 backend, if you enabled `use_lockfile = true`:\n\n```hcl\nterraform {\n  backend \"s3\" {\n    # Remove or set to false\n    # use_lockfile = false\n  }\n}\n\n# Then reconfigure\nterraform init -reconfigure\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Summary of Breaking Changes\n\n| Change | Impact | Required Action |\n|--------|--------|-----------------|\n| S3 backend deprecated IAM attributes removed | All S3 backends with IAM role assumption must be updated | Migrate to `assume_role` block |\n| Moved blocks require `resource.` prefix for reserved keywords | Any `moved` blocks referencing resources with reserved keyword names | Add `resource.` prefix to addresses |\n| Sensitive marks now propagate in conditional expressions | May see more values marked as sensitive | Review plan output; use `nonsensitive()` if needed |\n| Ephemeral resources/values introduced | New feature, optional adoption | Plan migration for temporary credentials |\n\n---\n\n## 7.
